    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/70365560-michelle-hoult"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1502664826i/70365560._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/70365560-michelle-hoult">Michelle Hoult</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    There aren't pictures all over the house. Hal has always assumed the woman who raised her was her biological mother, so when she sees the photo, she a<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    There aren't pictures all over the house. Hal has always assumed the woman who raised her was her biological mother, so when she sees the photo, she assumes the dark-haired one is her mother, Maggie. It's only when she looks at the older photos in the album that she realizes Maud is the dark haired one. While she asks Abel who the other woman is, she doesn't point to either woman, because at that point, she's still pretending that Maud is her mother. The line about Maggie staring at the photographer is because Ezra set up the camera on a timer. Abel tells her that when she asks later, but she doesn't believe him, because at that point she is thinking his boyfriend, Edward, is her father and Abel is protecting him.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

<div id="review_2351080638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2351080638" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2351080638?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2351080638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3969331841565467235"><blockquote>
  <i>There was a lock on the door. Two, in fact. They were long, thick bolts, top and bottom.<br/>But they were on the outside.</i>
</blockquote><br/>This book was so creepy. In a great way. I'm really glad I finally broke down and read a Ruth Ware book.<br/><br/>My sister is a huge Ruth Ware fan so I, of course, in true sibling fashion, had to decide I hated her on principal and avoid all her previous books. Okay, I'm joking, but <a href='https://www.instagram.com/chelsey_adele/' rel='nofollow noopener'>that dirty wench</a> spoiled most of the endings to the others so I have had to bag an arc to be able to rea</span>
  <span id="freeText3969331841565467235" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>There was a lock on the door. Two, in fact. They were long, thick bolts, top and bottom.<br />But they were on the outside.</i>
</blockquote><br />This book was so creepy. In a great way. I'm really glad I finally broke down and read a Ruth Ware book.<br /><br />My sister is a huge Ruth Ware fan so I, of course, in true sibling fashion, had to decide I hated her on principal and avoid all her previous books. Okay, I'm joking, but <a href="https://www.instagram.com/chelsey_adele/" rel="nofollow noopener">that dirty wench</a> spoiled most of the endings to the others so I have had to bag an arc to be able to read this spoiler-free. And I loved it! <b>Such a delicious, hard-to-put-down mystery.</b><br /><br />What's not to love about old dark secrets, even older darker houses, and mysterious family legacies?<br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36373481.The_Death_of_Mrs__Westaway" title="The Death of Mrs. Westaway by Ruth Ware" rel="nofollow noopener">The Death of Mrs. Westaway</a>, Hal reads tarot cards on Brighton pier and struggles daily to pay the bills and find food to keep her going. This has been her life since the death of her mother a few years earlier. So when she receives a letter bequeathing a large inheritance to her, she decides to accept, even though she knows it must be a mistake.<br /><br />Hal travels down to the English coast and meets her "family". She is taken to the huge, cold and gloomy Trepassen house-- a place that holds a thousand secrets within its walls. It soon becomes clear to Hal that something is not quite right, that she may indeed have a history entwined with the Westaways, and that someone in Trepassen house is determined to keep the past hidden, whatever it costs.<br /><br />Ware builds up to her reveals so well. She had me on a hook the entire time I was reading, pacing the novel just right, gradually pulling back the curtain (and years) on the mystery. She remembers that the <i>whys</i> of mysteries are so much more important than the <i>whos</i> (because, come on, there's only so many people it can be, right?). <br /><br />There's just this <b>overwhelming feeling of wrongness</b> that permeates the novel, and it makes for a very compelling read. Though this is not a supernatural story, the author plays with your mind just enough to have you questioning your own sense of reality and logic. I love the ghostly <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37034.The_Woman_in_Black" title="The Woman in Black by Susan Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">The Woman in Black</a> vibe, the creepy old housekeeper, and the isolated setting. <br /><blockquote><i>The cards tell you nothing you don’t already know. </i>It was her mother’s voice, steady in her ear.<i> They have no power, remember that. They can’t reveal any secrets or dictate the future. All they can do is show you what you already know.</i></blockquote><br />I especially love how the tarot aspect plays into everything, showing symbolism in everyday objects such as the four cups on the table. As Hal's mother noted, the cards are not magic or psychic, but they do have a way of pointing you in a certain direction, making you notice things you'd ignored before. It was very effective.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3969331841565467235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2334932627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8399837112998672050">This is one of those books that relies on conversations not had, coincidences, misunderstandings or misexplainations, and a serious dose of people seemingly deliberately taking the least likely option necessitated by the evidence. If, while reading, I have to whisper 'are you serious?' to myself repeatedly as I follow the main character's journey, it is not a good thing. The author seems to have thought out a story then said to herself, how can I make this needlessly messy so it looks cleverer? </span>
  <span id="freeText8399837112998672050" style="display:none">This is one of those books that relies on conversations not had, coincidences, misunderstandings or misexplainations, and a serious dose of people seemingly deliberately taking the least likely option necessitated by the evidence. If, while reading, I have to whisper 'are you serious?' to myself repeatedly as I follow the main character's journey, it is not a good thing. The author seems to have thought out a story then said to herself, how can I make this needlessly messy so it looks cleverer? Whole sections are entirely unnecessary and the book doesn't know whether it's trying to be gothic horror, an Agatha Christie style whodunnit, or psychological thriller, ensuring that it does none of them well.<br /><br />Still, it seems to be only me who thinks this way so *shrugs shoulders and walks away*....<br /><br /><br /><br />ARC via Netgalley</span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320129587?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      Simon &amp; Schuster Goodreads
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320129587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer975599366283914086"><i>"Centered around slow building suspense and tension you could cut with a knife, gothic thriller THE DEATH OF MRS. WESTAWAY is Ms. Ware's most ambitious and entertaining novel to date."</i><br/><br/>All hail Queen Ruth Ware! It's no secret that lady authors have been taking over the psychological thriller scene in the past decade (GiRl PoWeR), but there are a handful that seem to come to the forefront when planning out what we want to read over the summer months. Ms. Ware has been a highly coveted name in rece</span>
  <span id="freeText975599366283914086" style="display:none"><i>"Centered around slow building suspense and tension you could cut with a knife, gothic thriller THE DEATH OF MRS. WESTAWAY is Ms. Ware's most ambitious and entertaining novel to date."</i><br /><br />All hail Queen Ruth Ware! It's no secret that lady authors have been taking over the psychological thriller scene in the past decade (GiRl PoWeR), but there are a handful that seem to come to the forefront when planning out what we want to read over the summer months. Ms. Ware has been a highly coveted name in recent years and for good reason; whether you have read her books from the beginning or are just jumping into her scene, you'll note that she writes a gripping novel with memorable characters and breathtaking atmosphere. While all of her novels would be shelved clearly under the psych thriller persona, this one shined more brightly than the rest, at least in my opinion, due to it's departure into the gothic suspense territory.<br /><br />I'm a huge fan of stories where the atmosphere is as formidable a character as the people who are making the action happen. <i>The Death Of Mrs. Westaway</i> was the perfect example of such a tale, and the oppressive setting ramps up the unsettled feeling in the reader from the very first page. I almost felt that this book gave off some serious Agatha Christie vibes, but with a modern flair. The slow burning mystery portion of the novel was fantastic; it's not so much about the "who" but the "why" and the "how" in this case. The unraveling of what's really going on had a very traditionalist feel to it, and I wholly embraced the slight changes in the story that brought us to a climax that was both intense and gripping.<br /><br />Do you like playing detective, perhaps finding clues along the journey of your reading experience? Then you'll most certainly LOVE <i>The Death Of Mrs. Westaway</i>. The devil is in the details, and that phrase couldn't ring more true than it does in this particular story. I had such a blast trying to solve the mystery in all it's parts and found, while a slow burn through and through, I couldn't put it down due to the story's compulsive nature. Dark, unsettling, and full of unexpected twists, Ms. Ware has created one of the "it" stories of 2018. Highly recommended!<br /><br /><i>*Many thanks to the publisher for providing my review copy.</i><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="975599366283914086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2386063313" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2386063313" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2386063313?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2386063313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1643024388509072951"><b>
  <i> NEVER BELIEVE YOUR OWN LIES. </i>
</b><i>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <b>
    <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway is a cleverly crafted atmospheric mystery fueled by deceit. Since I was not a fan of The Lying Game, I was hesitant to read this, but I am so glad I did!</i>
  </b>
</i> <br/><br/>Struggling tarot card reader, Hal, aka Harriet Westaway, finds herself in a moral quandary when she receives a letter naming her as a beneficiary in her grandmother’s will. She believes a mistake has been made as her grandparents died long before she was born. Even t</span>
  <span id="freeText1643024388509072951" style="display:none"><b>
  <i> NEVER BELIEVE YOUR OWN LIES. </i>
</b><i>
  <br />
  <br />
  <b>
    <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway is a cleverly crafted atmospheric mystery fueled by deceit. Since I was not a fan of The Lying Game, I was hesitant to read this, but I am so glad I did!</i>
  </b>
</i> <br /><br />Struggling tarot card reader, Hal, aka Harriet Westaway, finds herself in a moral quandary when she receives a letter naming her as a beneficiary in her grandmother’s will. She believes a mistake has been made as her grandparents died long before she was born. Even though she knows that what she is doing is wrong, she is so desperate for money that she decides to travel to the funeral and play the role of the rightful heir. <br /><br />Hal travels to eerie Trepassen House, her “late grandmother’s” crumbling estate. She thinks that she is only going to inherit some money, but she soon learns that she has been left much more. At the estate, she meets her “uncles” and uses her keen observation skills to learn more about the creepy family that inhabited Trepassen. When Hal realizes that she has a legit family connection to these Westaways, she begins to dig for more information which leads her into grave danger.<br /><br /><b>The mystery surrounding Hal’s past kept me intrigued, but it was really Hal’s character that kept me turning pages. </b> Her character is what I loved most about this book. Hal has spent most of her life observing vs. being the center of attention, which has enabled her to master reading people. She can use this skill to deceive, but she has a generous nature. At the same time, she is also fighting to survive and must take what she can. <b>She is often referred to be as being mousy or weak, but her character exemplifies the notion that those who observe are more powerful than those who need to be the center of attention.</b><br /><br />Trepassen House also plays a large role. The thickly woven atmosphere surrounding the house transported me. Even though the events take place in the current moment, I felt like I had gone back in time while reading this as it is reminiscent of classic mysteries.The tarot card readings and the constant presence of magpies also contributed to this feeling.<br /><br /><b>This is not a book focused on fast-paced action, but rather on slowly unveiling the nuances surrounding the mystery. </b> Subtle clues are planted throughout, but all does not come together until the end. This is a mystery with many layers; I found it to be intriguing, intelligent, and entertaining. I was satisfied with how things played out. <b>The Death of Mrs. Westaway is one of my favorite reads of 2018! I recommend for those who enjoy slow-burn classic mysteries. </b><br /><br /> I received a copy of this book from NetGalley and Gallery Books in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1643024388509072951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2321870162" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2321870162" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2321870162?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781508251712" href="/book/show/36374452-the-death-of-mrs-westaway">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2321870162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2077279005906912878">This twisted tale of long-buried secrets is set at a <b>decrepit estate property, where the coldness gets under your skin,</b> and is the epitome of dreary gothic vibes.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540142630ra/26480716.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I went into this hoping for a solid <b>gothic atmosphere,</b> I mean, look at that cover.<br/><br/>I was hoping it would pull me under with the weight of it and <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i> did not disappoint in that regard.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597976120ra/29994730.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Our main character, Harriet 'Hal' Westaway, is a young woman down on her luck since the unfortunate hit-and-run death of her beloved </span>
  <span id="freeText2077279005906912878" style="display:none">This twisted tale of long-buried secrets is set at a <b>decrepit estate property, where the coldness gets under your skin,</b> and is the epitome of dreary gothic vibes.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540142630ra/26480716.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I went into this hoping for a solid <b>gothic atmosphere,</b> I mean, look at that cover.<br><br>I was hoping it would pull me under with the weight of it and <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i> did not disappoint in that regard.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597976120ra/29994730.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Our main character, Harriet 'Hal' Westaway, is a young woman down on her luck since the unfortunate hit-and-run death of her beloved mother. <br><br>One day, when she is at her lowest, a letter arrives announcing that her Grandmother, Hester Westaway, has passed and Hal is a named as a Beneficiary in her will. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457314602ra/18345434.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hal's presence is requested at the Solicitor's Office during the reading of said will. <br><br>Knowing it must be a mistake, her Grandparents died years ago, she decides nonetheless to go pretend to be the Harriet Westaway named in the letter, because, what could go wrong?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587847078ra/29357344.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At most she is expecting a small financial payout that will allow her to pay off some debt and perhaps live a little more comfortably. <br><br>Never in her wildest dreams could she have imagined what would take place once she entered into this dangerous game.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1535049772ra/26185286.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The family she meets upon traveling to the Westaway estate, <i>Trepassen House</i>, is hella eccentric and it was a ton of fun reading along as the truth unfolds. <br><br>Again, to me the <b>setting and atmosphere of this were fantastic</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587302258ra/29319628.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I could picture the cold, the snow, the eerie lake, the attic room with the bars on the windows; the estate was brought to life within the pages. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545057429ra/26760432.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I live for that in a story. At times, I felt I knew the answer to the mystery and I was correct on parts of it, but it was so twisted it was hard to tell until the final reveal whether I was on the right track or not. Truly a lot of fun to read.<br><br>I would definitely recommend this book to anyone who likes gothic vibes weaved into their Mystery-Thrillers. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1585064976ra/29160779.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My only slight criticism was that the beginning was a little slow. <br><br>I had this same feeling while reading, <i>The Woman in Cabin 10</i>, but luckily, for me, the introductory portion of this story didn't drag quite as much as that one. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454955908ra/18034498.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In the end, I am so happy that I picked this one up and I will definitely continue reading Ware's books in future. <br><br>If this one is any sign, it's that her works are getting stronger and stronger!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1539204530ra/26431201.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2077279005906912878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2326571504" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2326571504" />
    <a title="j e w e l s" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s"><img alt="j e w e l s" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552606306p2/68216634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2326571504?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=books-bejeweled">books-bejeweled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2326571504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13067722197244882162"><b>FIVE STARS</b><br/><br/>So, here's the thing. You can't really compare Ruth Ware to any contemporary writers. The pure "old-fashioned-ness" of her writing style is so refreshing that it comes across as modern. Weird, huh? You gotta go way back to find Ware's influences. Yep, that's Daphne Du Maurier, Agatha Christie and Patricia Highsmith. <br/><br/>These fantastic female authors constructed some of the best psychological suspense novels ever written, but they aren't quickly devoured like a lot of this genre's current </span>
  <span id="freeText13067722197244882162" style="display:none"><b>FIVE STARS</b><br /><br />So, here's the thing. You can't really compare Ruth Ware to any contemporary writers. The pure "old-fashioned-ness" of her writing style is so refreshing that it comes across as modern. Weird, huh? You gotta go way back to find Ware's influences. Yep, that's Daphne Du Maurier, Agatha Christie and Patricia Highsmith. <br /><br />These fantastic female authors constructed some of the best psychological suspense novels ever written, but they aren't quickly devoured like a lot of this genre's current output. Fine literature like fine wine requires some savoring time. <br /><br />Sniff, sip and swish this one around your mouth a few times. What's the hurry? Just sit back with your glass, soak up the formidable atmosphere, and enjoy the leisurely experience. <br /><br /><b>This is by far the best of Ware's novels. THE DEATH OF MRS. WESTAWAY is the book I have been waiting for Ware to create!! It is an immediate classic and the story of mistaken identity is an absolute perfect fit to Ware's charming, gothic style.</b><br /><br /><i>Loved the book, but I did not enjoy the audiobook version. Imogen Church is so wonderful when she is straight reading the book. However, there are numerous characters in this one and the overacted, squealing voices she portrays are just cringe inducing. Also, Ware uses the old diary device prominently in this story and I was confused so many times while listening (is this now? or reading from the diary again?). Ugh, I hate that I can't hear italics!😂😂 I went with Kindle in the end and was so glad I switched.</i><br /><br />THE DEATH OF MRS. WESTAWAY is not in the least “action packed”, but it is thoughtfully creepy and has so many twists in store for you. Wait for a thunderstorm. Break out the Courvoisier. Light some candles and crack open this beautiful, haunting and dark novel...just don't be in a rush! It's meant to be enjoyed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13067722197244882162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2377282944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2377282944" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2377282944?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2377282944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10843606475015427330">Ruth Ware writes an eerie, atmospheric and dark twisted murder mystery in the style of the golden age of crime classics with elements of the gothic. 21 year old Harriet 'Hal' Westaway lost her mother in a hit and run car accident, and took up the mantle of becoming a tarot reader at the Brighton Pier. Alone in the world, she is in dire financial straits, owing money to unscrupulous loan sharks, and facing a bleak and unpromising future. Out of the blue, she receives a letter that tells her of an</span>
  <span id="freeText10843606475015427330" style="display:none">Ruth Ware writes an eerie, atmospheric and dark twisted murder mystery in the style of the golden age of crime classics with elements of the gothic. 21 year old Harriet 'Hal' Westaway lost her mother in a hit and run car accident, and took up the mantle of becoming a tarot reader at the Brighton Pier. Alone in the world, she is in dire financial straits, owing money to unscrupulous loan sharks, and facing a bleak and unpromising future. Out of the blue, she receives a letter that tells her of an inheritance left to her by grandmother, Hester Mary Westaway, which she knows is an error, as both of her grandparents have been dead for a while. Her predicament and circumstances drive her to fraudulently pursue the inheritance, as she attends the funeral and travels to Cornwall to the huge and dilapidated Trepassen House, surrounded ominously by magpies. It doesn't take her long to become aware that something is terribly wrong. This is a story of a dysfunctional family, sibling conflicts and rivalry, intrigue, legacies and buried secrets from the past.<br /><br />Placed in the attic room, Hal faces hostility from all quarters, apart from Ezra. The elderly, menacing and strange Mrs Warren, the housekeeper appears to have own secrets as well as knowing secrets of others. Hal embarks on a search for the truth aided by her trusty tarot cards, as she wonders what her mother's involvement with the family is. As the past threatens to reveal itself, Hal has to draw on her inner resources as danger swirls around her. Hal is a flawed character, who you can forgive her deceptions, given the precarious nature of her finances. She is brave and courageous in the face of the dark Trepassen House and all the secrets held within its walls. Ware gives us a well plotted tale with rich evocative descriptions. This is a creepy, absorbing and entertaining read which I thoroughly enjoyed with its echoes of Rebecca, Agatha Christie and more. Many thanks to Random House Vintage for an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10843606475015427330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2340760228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2340760228" />
    <a title="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books"><img alt="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562505567p2/57632045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2340760228?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" href="/user/show/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books">Mackenzie - PhDiva Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books?shelf=2018-psychological-thrillers">2018-psychological-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2340760228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1213135973056828105">This book had me completely hooked from page one! <br/><br/>I have to give this 5 glowing stars 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟 for Ruth Ware—who if I’m being honest never disappoints me! This book was positively haunting!!! It was spooky yet meaningful, with lovely prose and compelling plot twists. I cannot recommend it enough!<br/><br/>I finished this book last night. It was one of those books that I stayed up late on a work night to finish, because I was so invested in the story. Hal’s dilemma had me completely immersed in the book. I th</span>
  <span id="freeText1213135973056828105" style="display:none">This book had me completely hooked from page one! <br /><br />I have to give this 5 glowing stars 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟 for Ruth Ware—who if I’m being honest never disappoints me! This book was positively haunting!!! It was spooky yet meaningful, with lovely prose and compelling plot twists. I cannot recommend it enough!<br /><br />I finished this book last night. It was one of those books that I stayed up late on a work night to finish, because I was so invested in the story. Hal’s dilemma had me completely immersed in the book. I think most readers will find themselves wondering what they would do if they were in Hal’s position! One thing that Ruth Ware does so well in this book (and in her previous work) is to write about characters that are cut off from society in some way. Sometimes this is done through a setting or an experience, and other times it is done through their social predicament. Hal fell into the latter category, with a dash of the first. <br /><br />What I love about the way Ruth Ware isolates characters is how it makes you forget the noise of the rest of the world. It’s easy to put yourself in their shoes, because she writes in a way that their problem is so isolated, that it shines right off of the page. Hal’s predicament felt like it became my predicament! Hal’s strength, worries, and ideas felt like my own. I was able to fully empathize with her, and root for her along the way. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>The promenade was empty, and the woman had disappeared into the darkness as if made from rain herself.</b>
</i><br /><br />Hal is alone in the world. Imagine being a young woman, raised by a single mother and with no other family, and then your mother passes away in a horrible accident. Hal has no money, no family, and no friends. All she has left from her mother is her Tarot Booth on the Promenade—named Madame Margarida, after her mother—and the strength to survive instilled in her since childhood. But what Hal also has is a debt that is hard to repay. Surviving comes at a cost, and Hal has run out of options. And then one day, a letter arrives…<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Don’t fall into the trap of believing your own lies.</b>
</i><br /><br />The letter informs Hal that she is set to receive some inheritance from the late Mrs. Westaway, her grandmother. The letter is addressed to Hal by name, and yet Hal knows it cannot be true. You see, Hal knows her grandparents all died long ago on her mother’s side, and the letter references Mrs. Westaway being her maternal grandmother. Still, with debt piling up higher and no chance to repay it, Hal wonders if her career of reading others and telling them what they need to hear might be just the thing to help her play the game long enough to earn a bit of inheritance.<br /><br />As Hal begins her journey to Trespassen House, she finds herself in over her head. It’s one thing to imagine taking a bit of money from those with plenty, but it’s another to place yourself in the center of someone else’s grief. The other Westaways are real people. And yet, there are many secrets in the home. Hal finds herself wondering if she isn’t the only person hiding something. And what will be the cost if those secrets come out?<br /><br /><i>
  <b>I can feel it—my secret—burning me up from the inside.</b>
</i><br /><br />I have to gush for a moment about the settings in this book. Ruth Ware uses such descriptive language, and this book takes place in some truly fantastic settings. From the spooky, abandoned promenade, to the bare apartment, to the dark mansion—I fell in love with the locations described in this book! I could imagine the settings so vivdly, as though I was there myself. I also loved the opening chapters on Hal’s work in the Tarot booth, and the people and settings she interacts with. I won’t spoil them, but they jumped off of the page for me.<br /><br />The duality in Hal was also a high point for me. Hal is physically meek, but she has an inner strength. The way Hal has learned to play weaker than she is, and then her shows of surprising resilience and bravery were so wonderful. Hal is an easy character to admire and to root for. Hal is someone who has been cast aside in every way, but she has never allowed it to diminish her. Hal is caring but self-preserving. Hal is honest but deceptive. Hal is calculating but impulsive.<br /><br />Many readers will enjoy this book, and I recommend it highly.<br /><br />I am so grateful to NetGalley, to Ruth Ware, and to Gallery/Scout Press for the opportunity to read an advanced copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />See my review (and more!) here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://novelbutnice.blogspot.com/2018/03/review-death-of-mrs-westaway.html">http://novelbutnice.blogspot.com/2018...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1213135973056828105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2330592012" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2330592012" />
    <a title="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16912659-dorie---cats-books"><img alt="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550077760p2/16912659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2330592012?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)" href="/user/show/16912659-dorie---cats-books">Dorie  - Cats&amp;Books :)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16912659-dorie---cats-books?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16912659-dorie---cats-books?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16912659-dorie---cats-books?shelf=netgalley-feedback">netgalley-feedback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2330592012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2312847281090873153">***STILL MY FAVORITE RUTH WARE NOVEL***<br/><br/>After “The Lying Game” which was a little disappointing to me, I was thoroughly thrilled and engrossed in this new book. Ms. Ware has again written a twisty, dark, atmospheric thriller, this time throwing family, inheritance and sibling rivalry into the brew.<br/><br/>Hal Westaway is still reeling from the death of her mother three months previously. She had to forgo her plans to attend college in order to take up her mother’s tarot reading kiosk on the pier in order</span>
  <span id="freeText2312847281090873153" style="display:none">***STILL MY FAVORITE RUTH WARE NOVEL***<br /><br />After “The Lying Game” which was a little disappointing to me, I was thoroughly thrilled and engrossed in this new book. Ms. Ware has again written a twisty, dark, atmospheric thriller, this time throwing family, inheritance and sibling rivalry into the brew.<br /><br />Hal Westaway is still reeling from the death of her mother three months previously. She had to forgo her plans to attend college in order to take up her mother’s tarot reading kiosk on the pier in order to pay the bills. Still she fell short and she make an enormous mistake, borrowing money from someone who was beginning to put pressure on her to pay back the loan with lots of interest and even more threats, bodily threats!<br /><br />While dealing with all of this and what her next step will be she gets a letter that she is heir to a substantial inheritance from her grandmother, Mrs. Westaway. Hal never knew that she had a grandmother and really thinks that there is a mix up but as she is pinned against the wall with the threat from her loan shark, she makes the decision to go to the funeral and see what the inheritance is all about. She is hoping for a few thousand pounds to help her get cleared of debt and start fresh.<br /><br />Once at Trepassen house, a falling down, once gorgeous estate, she discoveres that her inheritance is much more than just some money and her “uncles” are none too happy about it, with the exception of Ezra who seems to take her under his wing. The house lends a lot of creepiness to the story, including the terrible attic room which Hal is now sleeping in, with it’s bolts on the outside of the door and it’s message scratched into the window.<br /><br />Most of the family, however, embraces her as the daughter of their long lost sister and seem ready to accept her into the fold. Once the will is read, however, Hal is not so sure she wants any part of this, thinking she has perhaps dug herself into a really dark hole. Then she decides she will “take this step by step...with the slow, measured pace of a reading. She had to turn each card as it came, consider it, find it’s place in the story . . . . . only the next card was not a card at all, it was a photograph. the photograph . . . .”<br /><br />There are lots of characters quite well developed including the cranky, constantly lurking, Mrs. Warren, who has been the housekeeper since the uncles were children. She seems to know all of the secrets but seems to be biding her time, does she have a secret of her own? <br /><br />Mystery/thriller fans are going to love this new book, I did! The only thing that brought it down to a 4 was the fact that I figured out who the “bad guy” was and most of the mystery long before it was revealed. Still the ending is a great one and I loved every minute of this novel.<br /><br />Many thanks to the publisher and Edelweiss for an ARC of this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2312847281090873153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2430208191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2430208191" />
    <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read"><img alt="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580849831p2/24156068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2430208191?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read">Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781501151842" href="/book/show/38950501-the-death-of-mrs-westaway">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2430208191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8389469269692104030"><b>One for sorrow. Two for Joy. Three [stars] for Ruth Ware's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36373481.The_Death_of_Mrs__Westaway' title='The Death of Mrs. Westaway by Ruth Ware' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</a>!!!</b> <br/><br/>Harriet (Hal) Westaway grew up with a loving mother in a tiny flat, until every child's worst nightmare comes to fruition. In one fateful moment, Hal loses her mother and the only security and family she has ever known. Having spent the last few years adjusting to such a life altering change, she has settled into living day-to-day working as a tarot card reader on a pier. Hal is running low on cash, she's go</span>
  <span id="freeText8389469269692104030" style="display:none"><b>One for sorrow. Two for Joy. Three [stars] for Ruth Ware's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36373481.The_Death_of_Mrs__Westaway" title="The Death of Mrs. Westaway by Ruth Ware" rel="nofollow noopener">The Death of Mrs. Westaway</a>!!!</b> <br /><br />Harriet (Hal) Westaway grew up with a loving mother in a tiny flat, until every child's worst nightmare comes to fruition. In one fateful moment, Hal loses her mother and the only security and family she has ever known. Having spent the last few years adjusting to such a life altering change, she has settled into living day-to-day working as a tarot card reader on a pier. Hal is running low on cash, she's got loan sharks hunting her down like Jaws on Amity Island. <br /><br />Out of nowhere, Hal receives a mysterious letter bequeathing her an inheritance from a wealthy woman she is told is her grandmother. Hal knows an entirely different story of her upbringing, her grandparents and her entire life - she knows this letter was not meant for her. Despite this, her desperation leads her to attending the funeral, attempting to con this family into believing she is who they say she is. From here, things <i>slowly</i> descend into mayhem. <br /><br /><b>You can’t influence fate, or change what’s out of your control. But you can choose what you yourself do with the cards you’re dealt.</b><br /><br />Hal was by far my favorite part of this story. She was strong-willed, smart, and a genuinely likable character. Mystery / thriller novels fall short for me a bit when they rely solely on <i>interesting</i> over <i>likable</i> characters and I appreciate that Ware didn't fall into the unreliable narrator trope here. Ware did an exceptional job of showing how things snowballed with Hal, and despite making a semi-shifty choice in trying to defraud this family, you could empathize and understand her plight. <br /><br />However, past Hal, none of the characters held much depth for me. The banter between the Westaway family fell flat and I don't feel like there was a lot of development into who they were as people and what had brought them to this point and their animosity towards the situation. This read less like a mystery and more like a family drama but there wasn't enough back story to understand the intricacies at play. We are given Hal's sole POV with a few diary entries from before she was born thrown in. These diary entries are really the only look into the past we get - aside from a few conversations between family members. I would've loved to have seen just a bit more to fully develop that plot line. <br /><br /><b>She had discovered that the most important truths often lay in what people didn’t say, and learned to read the secrets that they hid in plain sight, in their faces, and in their clothes, and in the expressions that flitted across their faces when they thought no one was watching.</b><br /><br />In the end, this was a disappointment for me because I felt like there was so much <b>promise</b> here and I was a bit let down. The beginning draws the reader right in with intrigue and mystery but this quickly plateaus for what felt like a large portion of the book. Things don't really pick back up until the last 50 or so pages and then I ran into some implausibility issues that suffered due to a lack of development into the character. That being said, the final few twists were a complete knock-out I did not see coming from a mile away!<br /><br />I completed this as a Traveling Friends read and I can definitely see why this book appeals to so many, it just wasn't my particular brand of story. Anyone interested in slow burn mysteries, family sagas and atmospheric, gothic vibes would likely enjoy this story. Ware clearly has her writing chops well honed, despite this one falling a bit short for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8389469269692104030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2426012173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2426012173" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2426012173?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2426012173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1110111666816337311"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539283940i/26435592._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Seven for a secret, never to be told.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>This was my first Ruth Ware book, but sadly it wasn’t a hit with me. But looking at my friend’s reviews, I do think I might be in the minority with my feelings. I will say that the atmosphere was eerie and perfect. I will also say that the writing and prose was beautiful. But I’m not someone who reads a lot of thrillers or mysteries, but even I could see all the reveals in this one coming a mile away. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“One for Joy. One for love. One for </i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1110111666816337311" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539283940i/26435592._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Seven for a secret, never to be told.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This was my first Ruth Ware book, but sadly it wasn’t a hit with me. But looking at my friend’s reviews, I do think I might be in the minority with my feelings. I will say that the atmosphere was eerie and perfect. I will also say that the writing and prose was beautiful. But I’m not someone who reads a lot of thrillers or mysteries, but even I could see all the reveals in this one coming a mile away. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“One for Joy. One for love. One for the future.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i> is a story of a girl named Hal who has been grieving the loss of her mother for the past three years. She has had to take up the mantle of her mother’s psychic readings and tarot spreads for the community, making ends meet, and barely being able to hide from the loan sharks who she received money from when she was desperate. But she thinks her luck could change the day that she receives a letter, letting her know about the death of a woman she has never known and an inheritance that could not only solve her money problems, but change her life forever. <br><br>Hal feels like she is good enough at reading people, and telling them what they want to hear, that she might actually stand a chance at convincing them that she is a long lost relative, deserving of a fortune. So, Hal uses the very last of her money to attend the funeral of this mysterious woman she has never known, and travels to the estate, Trepassen. But she soon realizes that her mother has visited this place before, and Hal desperately tries to find out what went on over two decades ago that eventually led to her mother not only fleeing, but to never mention any of her past to Hal. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Never believe your own lies…”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>We also are able to see actual glimpses of the past, and events that happened at Trepassen that help piece together everything a bit more. And Ruth Ware is able to add some really amazing, and really creepy, parallels that make you feel really unsettled while reading. Again, the atmosphere of this book is really well done, and I couldn’t help feeling claustrophobic in that attic myself. <br><br>This all sounds super good right? Possibly haunted house? Unsolved murders? Family mysteries? Tarot readings? But that’s about where the coolness ends; with the premise. Hal leads the reader to believe she is so very perceptive, but she literally ignores every single thing that would help her unravel this mystery. And not to get into spoiler territory, but you couldn’t have paid me enough to stay in that attic! Especially after the light, the window, the attempted murder. Like, Hal just ended up being another, typical, stupid character in another typical, stupid murder mystery. And I’m extra let down because I felt like this had so much potential. <br><br>And this story wraps up with so many loose ends! What happened to the loan sharks? What happened with the will? What happened with the rest of the family? What were her future plans? Why would a certain somebody help her when they had no real motive? I don’t know friends, but this was just a big letdown for me. <br><br>Overall, this was just an okay read for me. I didn’t dislike it, but I disliked more things about it than I liked. But again, I am totally in the minority with my feelings based on the Goodreads reviews I’ve been seeing. Another thing I’ll say is that this reminds me of an Agatha Christie novel, another author I’ve never really enjoyed. So, if you do – then I’d probably really recommend this one to you, too! <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><b>Content and trigger warnings</b> for harassment, anxiety, loss of a loved one, parental abuse, physical abuse, abandonment, captivity, and murder. <br><br>Buddy read for <a href="https://meltotheany.com/2018/09/24/fridayfrightathon-2018/" rel="nofollow noopener">#FridayFrightAThon</a> which I co-hosted with <a href="https://acourtofcrownsandquills.wordpress.com/2018/09/23/blanca-y-roja-by-anna-marie-mclemore/" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy @ A Court of Crowns and Quills</a>, <a href="https://pinotandpages247.wordpress.com/2018/09/23/arc-review-shadow-of-the-fox/" rel="nofollow noopener">Jen @ Pinot and Pages</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=otwtCWoDoNs" rel="nofollow noopener">Chelsea @ Chelsea Palmer</a>! 👻</span>

<div id="review_2300706174" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2300706174" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2300706174?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2300706174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4763386762620472512">The Death of Mrs. Westaway by Ruth Ware is a Gallery Scout publication. <br/><br/>When Harriet- aka- Hal, receives a mysterious letter informing her that she’s been named in her grandmothers will, and stands to receive a substantial sum of money, she knows immediately a mistake has been made. But, her Tarot Card Booth is not getting the bills paid and her creditors are breathing down her neck, some of which have become threatening. Facing a moral dilemma, with her back against a wall, Hal decides to take </span>
  <span id="freeText4763386762620472512" style="display:none">The Death of Mrs. Westaway by Ruth Ware is a Gallery Scout publication. <br /><br />When Harriet- aka- Hal, receives a mysterious letter informing her that she’s been named in her grandmothers will, and stands to receive a substantial sum of money, she knows immediately a mistake has been made. But, her Tarot Card Booth is not getting the bills paid and her creditors are breathing down her neck, some of which have become threatening. Facing a moral dilemma, with her back against a wall, Hal decides to take a chance and test the water by attending the funeral of her ‘grandmother’ – Mrs. Westaway. <br /><br />Once she’s made her fateful choice, her life as she knows it will never be the same again- if she survives…<br /><br />Well, I suppose it was bound to happen. I’ve really enjoyed Ware’s previous novels and I see that this one has been well received for the most part. But, for me this one was a bit flat. It took me an age to get into the story, and the tried and true attempts to build suspense, were too obvious to be effective. <br /><br />By all accounts, this book should have been right up my alley. The old house, the creepy housekeeper, the gathering of the suspects, and the moral issues are all elements I love in a good mystery/suspense novel. But, the pacing was just too slow, the characters were uninteresting, and the dialogue was a bit dull. I can’t really explain why this book didn’t resonate with me, but I just couldn’t get into it. The Magpie references seem to be a popular theme in books right now, but this time it didn’t impress me, and I mainly found it distracting. I guessed major parts of the mystery in advance, so the only thing propelling me forward was seeing how Hal discovered the truth and how it would come to an end. <br /><br />After giving it a few days, I think maybe it was more of a ‘it’s not you, it’s me’ situation. I was excited about the book, and the plot was original, but, it just didn’t grab me. It was okay, and I see why most of my GR friends loved this one. I’m disappointed that I can’t seem to muster that level of enthusiasm for the book, but believe me, it wasn’t from a lack of trying. <br />3 stars<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4763386762620472512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2312751189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2312751189" />
    <a title="JanB " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/260116-janb"><img alt="JanB " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527313486p2/260116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2312751189?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JanB " class="user" itemprop="url" name="JanB " href="/user/show/260116-janb">JanB </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2312751189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4702820798841057890">4.5 stars, rounded up. Read with the Traveling Friends group, this made for a fun discussion as we tried to piece together the clues and solve the mystery.<br/><br/>And what a twisty, fantastic story it was! An old crumbling estate, a malevolent housekeeper, a dysfunctional family, long-held family secrets, missing people…. all elements that I love in a tale that oozes a menacing gothic atmosphere.<br/><br/>The story opens with 21-year-old Hal, who was left all alone in the world 3 years ago after her mother’s deat</span>
  <span id="freeText4702820798841057890" style="display:none">4.5 stars, rounded up. Read with the Traveling Friends group, this made for a fun discussion as we tried to piece together the clues and solve the mystery.<br /><br />And what a twisty, fantastic story it was! An old crumbling estate, a malevolent housekeeper, a dysfunctional family, long-held family secrets, missing people…. all elements that I love in a tale that oozes a menacing gothic atmosphere.<br /><br />The story opens with 21-year-old Hal, who was left all alone in the world 3 years ago after her mother’s death. She was forced to set aside her plans of college and took over her mother’s job as a tarot card reader. Hal has difficulty making ends meet and has fallen victim to a loan shark, leaving her desperate. Her fortunes seem to take a turn for the better when a mysterious letter arrives. Hal has been named as a beneficiary in her grandmother's will. <br /><br />Too bad Mrs. Westaway isn’t her grandmother, but from her tarot card reading and dealings with the public, Hal knows how to read people and situations and is confident she can pull off the deception. What’s the harm in playing along and walking away with just a little money to help her through this rough patch? Hal hops on a train to attend the reading of the will and ends up staying with the Westaway family. From here, the tension and suspense made this an addictive read that I had difficulty putting down.<br /><br />I loved how the author dropped clues like bread crumbs throughout the novel, but it wasn’t until the end that the puzzle pieces clicked into place. I thought I had it figured out but turned out to be only partially right. I was pleasantly surprised - well done Ms. Ware! <br /><br />This book hooked me from page one right through to the end. Highly recommended for fans of an old-fashioned mystery, reminiscent of Agatha Christie.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4702820798841057890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2622643961384126533">I love Ruth Ware's books, and I found this one to be her best yet. It sees Hal, a young tarot card reader, summoned to the country as her grandmother had died. The only thing is Hal's grandparents had died many years before. However, as she is in debt and wondering where her next months rent money is coming from, she goes, with the idea of swindling the family. Yet as she gets to know the family she feels guilt ridden, and even though something seems off about the family, she can't pinpoint what</span>
  <span id="freeText2622643961384126533" style="display:none">I love Ruth Ware's books, and I found this one to be her best yet. It sees Hal, a young tarot card reader, summoned to the country as her grandmother had died. The only thing is Hal's grandparents had died many years before. However, as she is in debt and wondering where her next months rent money is coming from, she goes, with the idea of swindling the family. Yet as she gets to know the family she feels guilt ridden, and even though something seems off about the family, she can't pinpoint what it is. What are the families secrets? And who is hiding what? Several scenarios went through my head as I was racing through the book, and the final chapters were exceptional. Ruth Ware has crafted a superb thriller with this, what has to be the best book I have read so far this year. Highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_2312649156" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2312649156" />
    <a title="Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67496521-dennis"><img alt="Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597768154p2/67496521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2312649156?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dennis" href="/user/show/67496521-dennis">Dennis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=2018-pub">2018-pub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67496521-dennis?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2312649156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10050547410578348713">First and foremost, I'm happy to say that <b>RUTH WARE IS BACK!</b> I've been a fan of Ruth Ware since Day 1. <i>In a Dark, Dark Wood</i> was such a good debut light-mystery novel and <i>The Woman in Cabin 10</i> was one of my favorite mystery novels of all time. After my disappointment with <i>The Lying Game</i>, I still was hopeful for <b>
  <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i>
</b>. Ruth Ware went back to her roots with <b>
  <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i>
</b> and created a robust, multifaceted, and fascinating story. Seriously guys, I read this </span>
  <span id="freeText10050547410578348713" style="display:none">First and foremost, I'm happy to say that <b>RUTH WARE IS BACK!</b> I've been a fan of Ruth Ware since Day 1. <i>In a Dark, Dark Wood</i> was such a good debut light-mystery novel and <i>The Woman in Cabin 10</i> was one of my favorite mystery novels of all time. After my disappointment with <i>The Lying Game</i>, I still was hopeful for <b>
  <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i>
</b>. Ruth Ware went back to her roots with <b>
  <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i>
</b> and created a robust, multifaceted, and fascinating story. Seriously guys, I read this 360+ page book in one sitting! <br /><br />Harriet (Hal) Westaway is a young twenty-something year old tarot card reader in Brighton, England. She is struggling to pay the bills; barely making rent while her business is providing dismal financial stability. With loan sharks out to enforce their illegal and exploitative payment plans, Hal is looking for a light at the end of the tunnel. Her mother died years ago, and she has no family to lean on—she is utterly alone. As Hal checks her mail, she receives notice that her grandmother, Hester Mary Westaway, has recently passed away and has left Hal an inheritance of some kind. Hal believes this to be a clerical error of some kind because her grandparents have been dead for years. Desperate, Hal decides that she can fraudulently try and claim this inheritance as her own—she's been conning innocent people for years as a tarot card reader and this will just be another gig for her. <br /><br />When Hal arrives to the Westaway family home, she quickly finds herself immersed in a rich family history that quickly starts to crumble. Something is wrong with this family, but Hal just can't seem to grasp what is so concerning. In a world of family dynamics, betrayal, and greed; <b>
  <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i>
</b> delivers a realistic mystery crime-fiction novel that will keep you hooked from page one. <br /><br />I know it's lame to compare author's works to each other, but in order to show the reasoning behind my five-star rating for <b>
  <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i>
</b>, I'm going to have to tell you how this story differs from Ware's other works. <b>At its core, <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i> provides a lot more atmospheric undertones than anything she's ever produced. Its gothic atmosphere provides a higher level of suspense that I have yet to see in anything else.</b> This story is a lot more dense than <i>In a Dark, Dark Wood</i> and <i>The Woman in Cabin 10</i>; you can really see the progress Ruth Ware has made in her writing and she continually fine tunes it in this story. For about a good 30% of the book, we have the characterization of Hal set perfectly. At first, I immediately felt that this was going to be a slow burn novel, but I was wrong because everything comes full circle. We see Hal's desperation come to life and her willingness to deceive to survive. Hal is not the typical alcoholic unreliable narrator that we have come to <b>grow tired of in every suspense novel that has been published since 2015.</b> Hal is entertaining and honestly refreshing. When we meet the secondary characters, they are all unique and interesting in their own way. Each character in <b>
  <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i>
</b> is fully developed and multi-dimensional. <br /><br />After reading the synopsis, throw everything you think about Ruth Ware novels out the window. <b>
  <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i>
</b> will keep you guessing until the very end <i>(seriously, I thought the story was winding down and was completely thrown off by the end)</i>. <b>Thank you Scout Press/Gallery Books for my advanced copy in exchange for an honest review. <i>The Death of Mrs. Westaway</i> will be released May 29, 2018.</b><br /><br /><i>One for sorrow<br />Two for joy<br />Three for a girl<br />Four for a boy<br />Five for silver<br />Six for gold<br />Seven for a secret<br />Never to be told.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10050547410578348713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
